<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="background-color:#DCDCDC;">
<div>
<div class="plainlist">
<ul>
<li>Part of the <a href="/wiki/First_Chechen_War" title="First Chechen War">First Chechen War</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_of_Dagestan" title="War of Dagestan">War of Dagestan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Second_Chechen_War" title="Second Chechen War">Second Chechen War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Insurgency_in_the_North_Caucasus" title="Insurgency in the North Caucasus">Insurgency in the North Caucasus</a></li>

<p><b>Metrojet Flight 9268</b> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IATA_airline_designator" title="IATA airline designator">IATA</a>: <b>7K9268</b>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICAO_airline_designator" title="ICAO airline designator">ICAO</a>: <b>KGL9268</b>) was an international <a href="/wiki/Air_charter" title="Air charter">chartered passenger flight</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> operated by Russian airline <a href="/wiki/Metrojet_(Russian_airline)" title="Metrojet (Russian airline)">Kogalymavia</a> (branded as Metrojet). On 31 October 2015 at 06:13 local time <a href="/wiki/Egypt_Standard_Time" title="Egypt Standard Time">EST</a> (04:13 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FR24_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FR24-2">[2]</a></sup> an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321-231</a> operating the flight disintegrated above the northern <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">Sinai</a> following its departure from <a href="/wiki/Sharm_El_Sheikh_International_Airport" title="Sharm El Sheikh International Airport">Sharm El Sheikh International Airport</a>, Egypt, en route to <a href="/wiki/Pulkovo_Airport" title="Pulkovo Airport">Pulkovo Airport</a>, Saint Petersburg, Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ah_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-ah-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> All 217 passengers and seven crew members who were on board were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mchsvictims_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-mchsvictims-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Of those aboard, mostly tourists, there were 219 Russians, four Ukrainians, and one Belarusian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mchsvictims_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-mchsvictims-6">[6]</a></sup> The possibility that a <a href="/wiki/Bomb" title="Bomb">bomb</a> was put on the aircraft at Sharm El Sheikh led several countries to suspend flights to that airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto4_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-8">[8]</a></sup> With its death toll of 224 people,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mchsvictims_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-mchsvictims-6">[6]</a></sup> Flight 9268 is the deadliest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_disaster" title="Air disaster">air disaster</a> both in the history of Russian aviation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[a]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> and within Egyptian territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[b]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-12">[10]</a></sup> It is also the deadliest air disaster involving an aircraft from the Airbus A320 family,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[c]</a></sup> and the deadliest air disaster of 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[d]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RT_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-RT-15">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly after the crash, the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a> (ISIL)'s <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant_%E2%80%93_Sinai_Province" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant – Sinai Province">Sinai Branch</a>, previously known as <a href="/wiki/Ansar_Bait_al-Maqdis" title="Ansar Bait al-Maqdis">Ansar Bait al-Maqdis</a>, claimed responsibility for the incident, which occurred in the vicinity of the <a href="/wiki/Sinai_insurgency" title="Sinai insurgency">Sinai insurgency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto3_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-17">[13]</a></sup> ISIL claimed responsibility on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>, on video, and in a statement by <a href="/wiki/Abu_Osama_al-Masri" title="Abu Osama al-Masri">Abu Osama al-Masri</a>, the leader of the group's Sinai branch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leaderpost.com_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-leaderpost.com-19">[15]</a></sup> ISIL posted pictures of what it said was the bomb in <i><a href="/wiki/Dabiq_(magazine)" title="Dabiq (magazine)">Dabiq</a></i>, its online magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBTB_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-IBTB-20">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 4 November 2015, British and American authorities suspected that a bomb was responsible for the crash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US-UK_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-US-UK-21">[17]</a></sup> On 8 November 2015, an anonymous member of the Egyptian investigation team said the investigators were "90 percent sure" that the jet was brought down by a bomb. Lead investigator Ayman al-Muqaddam said that other possible causes of the crash included a <a href="/wiki/Jet_fuel" title="Jet fuel">fuel</a> <a href="/wiki/Explosion" title="Explosion">explosion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatigue_(material)" title="Fatigue (material)">metal fatigue</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">lithium batteries</a> overheating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto4_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-8">[8]</a></sup> The Russian <a href="/wiki/Federal_Security_Service" title="Federal Security Service">Federal Security Service</a> announced on 17 November that they were sure that it was a terrorist attack, caused by an <a href="/wiki/Improvised_explosive_device" title="Improvised explosive device">improvised bomb</a> containing the <a href="/wiki/TNT_equivalent" title="TNT equivalent">equivalent</a> of up to 1 kilogram (2.2 lb) of <a href="/wiki/Trinitrotoluene" title="Trinitrotoluene">TNT</a> that detonated during the flight. The Russians said they had found explosive residue as evidence. On 24 February 2016, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Egypt" title="President of Egypt">Egyptian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Abdel_Fattah_el-Sisi" title="Abdel Fattah el-Sisi">Abdel Fattah el-Sisi</a> acknowledged that terrorism caused the crash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-el-sisi_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-el-sisi-22">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft">Aircraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Aircraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A321-231,_Middle_East_Airlines_-_MEA_AN0094392.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="492" data-file-width="800" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Airbus_A321-231%2C_Middle_East_Airlines_-_MEA_AN0094392.jpg/220px-Airbus_A321-231%2C_Middle_East_Airlines_-_MEA_AN0094392.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Airbus_A321-231%2C_Middle_East_Airlines_-_MEA_AN0094392.jpg/330px-Airbus_A321-231%2C_Middle_East_Airlines_-_MEA_AN0094392.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Airbus_A321-231%2C_Middle_East_Airlines_-_MEA_AN0094392.jpg/440px-Airbus_A321-231%2C_Middle_East_Airlines_-_MEA_AN0094392.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Onur_Air_Airbus_A321_(TC-OAE)_at_Manchester_Airport.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2347" data-file-width="3912" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Onur_Air_Airbus_A321_%28TC-OAE%29_at_Manchester_Airport.jpg/220px-Onur_Air_Airbus_A321_%28TC-OAE%29_at_Manchester_Airport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Onur_Air_Airbus_A321_%28TC-OAE%29_at_Manchester_Airport.jpg/330px-Onur_Air_Airbus_A321_%28TC-OAE%29_at_Manchester_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Onur_Air_Airbus_A321_%28TC-OAE%29_at_Manchester_Airport.jpg/440px-Onur_Air_Airbus_A321_%28TC-OAE%29_at_Manchester_Airport.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A321-231,_MetroJet_JP7726808.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Airbus_A321-231%2C_MetroJet_JP7726808.jpg/220px-Airbus_A321-231%2C_MetroJet_JP7726808.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Airbus_A321-231%2C_MetroJet_JP7726808.jpg/330px-Airbus_A321-231%2C_MetroJet_JP7726808.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Airbus_A321-231%2C_MetroJet_JP7726808.jpg/440px-Airbus_A321-231%2C_MetroJet_JP7726808.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">The aircraft in previous service: first with <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Airlines" title="Middle East Airlines">Middle East Airlines</a> (top), then during its operation with <a href="/wiki/Onur_Air" title="Onur Air">Onur Air</a> (middle) and then in previous Metrojet livery with the <a href="/wiki/TUI_Group" title="TUI Group">TUI</a> logo (bottom)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The aircraft was an 18-year-old <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A321-231</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serial_code" title="Serial code">serial number</a> 663.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Airbus_press_release_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_press_release-23">[19]</a></sup> It was delivered to <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Airlines" title="Middle East Airlines">Middle East Airlines</a> in May 1997 with a <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_registration" title="Aircraft registration">registration code</a> of F-OHMP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[20]</a></sup> In 2003, it was leased by <a href="/wiki/Onur_Air" title="Onur Air">Onur Air</a> and, beginning in 2007, it was subleased to <a href="/wiki/Saudia" title="Saudia">Saudi Arabian Airlines</a> and other carriers. In April 2012, <a href="/wiki/Metrojet_(Russian_airline)" title="Metrojet (Russian airline)">Kolavia</a> acquired the aircraft with a new registration of EI-ETJ and transferred it to Kogalymavia in May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>The aircraft was powered by two <a href="/wiki/IAE_V2500" title="IAE V2500">IAE V2533</a> engines and configured to carry 220 passengers in an economy configuration plus crew seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[22]</a></sup> At the time of the crash, it was owned by <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>-based <a href="/wiki/AerCap" title="AerCap">AerCap</a> and leased to <a href="/wiki/Metrojet_(Russian_airline)" title="Metrojet (Russian airline)">Kolavia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[23]</a></sup> The aircraft had accumulated 56,000 flight hours on nearly 21,000 flights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Airbus_press_release_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_press_release-23">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 November 2001, while operating for <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Airlines" title="Middle East Airlines">Middle East Airlines</a> as F-OHMP, the aircraft suffered a <a href="/wiki/Tailstrike" title="Tailstrike">tailstrike</a> landing in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>. It was repaired and went back into service with the airline in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asn_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-asn-28">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crash">Crash</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Crash">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flight_7K9268_crash.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="286" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Flight_7K9268_crash.svg/170px-Flight_7K9268_crash.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Flight_7K9268_crash.svg/255px-Flight_7K9268_crash.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Flight_7K9268_crash.svg/340px-Flight_7K9268_crash.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flight_7K9268_crash.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The route of the aircraft. The black dot indicates the starting point of the flight; the red dot indicates the last position at which the aircraft was tracked.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Flight 9268 left Sharm El Sheikh airport at 05:50 <a href="/wiki/Egypt_Standard_Time" title="Egypt Standard Time">EST</a> (03:50 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FR24_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-FR24-2">[2]</a></sup> for <a href="/wiki/Pulkovo_Airport" title="Pulkovo Airport">Pulkovo Airport</a> in Saint Petersburg, Russia, with 217 passengers and seven crew members on board. The aircraft failed to make contact with Cyprus Air Traffic Control 23 minutes later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[25]</a></sup> Russia's <a href="/wiki/Federal_Air_Transport_Agency" title="Federal Air Transport Agency">Federal Air Transport Agency</a> confirmed the flight had disappeared from radar tracking, but there was initial confusion about whether the aircraft had crashed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sput_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sput-30">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_State_in_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State in Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State in Iraq and the Levant</a> branch in Egypt said that it brought down the airliner. Wassim Nasr, <a href="/wiki/France_24" title="France 24">France 24</a>’s expert on jihadi movements, said that the ISIL group has never claimed an attack they did not commit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto3_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-17">[13]</a></sup> Russian media outlets said that the pilot reported technical problems and had requested a landing at the nearest airport before the A321 went missing. This claim was disputed by other sources,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sputnik_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sputnik-31">[27]</a></sup> including the Egyptian authorities and subsequent analysis of the <a href="/wiki/Flight_recorder" title="Flight recorder">flight recorder</a> data confirmed that no distress or diversion request was given.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-32">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes1_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes1-33">[29]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_Civilian_Aviation_Ministry" title="Egyptian Civilian Aviation Ministry">Egyptian Civilian Aviation Ministry</a> issued a statement that indicated the flight was at an altitude of 31,000 ft (9,400 m) when it disappeared from radar screens after a steep descent of 5,000 ft (1,500 m) in one minute. <a href="/wiki/Flightradar24" title="Flightradar24">Flightradar24</a> shows the aircraft climbing to 33,500 ft (10,200 m) at 404 kn (748 km/h; 465 mph) before suddenly descending to 28,375 ft (8,649 m) at 62 kn (115 km/h; 71 mph) approximately 50 km (31 mi) north east of <a href="/wiki/Nekhel" title="Nekhel">Nekhel</a>, after which its position was no longer tracked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flirad-24_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-flirad-24-34">[30]</a></sup> All 224 passengers and crew died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes1_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes1-33">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> quoted an unnamed security officer as saying that the aircraft had been completely destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blive_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-blive-35">[31]</a></sup> Wreckage was scattered over 20 square kilometres (8 sq mi), with the forward section about 5 kilometres (3.1 mi) from the tail, indicating that the aircraft had broken up during flight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kramer1Nov_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kramer1Nov-36">[32]</a></sup> Aerial images of the wreckage broadcast on <a href="/wiki/RT_(TV_network)" title="RT (TV network)">RT</a> indicated that the wings were intact until impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Irving2015_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Irving2015-37">[33]</a></sup> The debris pattern, combined with an initial interpretation of the aircraft's abrupt changes in altitude and airspeed, reinforced the presumption that the aircraft's tail separated during flight and fell separately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Irving2015_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Irving2015-37">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Response">Response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flightradar24.com_-_flight_7K9268.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="586" data-file-width="812" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Flightradar24.com_-_flight_7K9268.png/220px-Flightradar24.com_-_flight_7K9268.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Flightradar24.com_-_flight_7K9268.png/330px-Flightradar24.com_-_flight_7K9268.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Flightradar24.com_-_flight_7K9268.png/440px-Flightradar24.com_-_flight_7K9268.png 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KGL_9268_FlightData.pdf"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1275" data-file-width="1650" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/KGL_9268_FlightData.pdf/page1-220px-KGL_9268_FlightData.pdf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/KGL_9268_FlightData.pdf/page1-330px-KGL_9268_FlightData.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/KGL_9268_FlightData.pdf/page1-440px-KGL_9268_FlightData.pdf.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KGL_9268_FlightData.pdf" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flight data received by <a href="/wiki/Flightradar24" title="Flightradar24">FlightRadar24.com</a> receivers since 04:12:00 UTC</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Shortly after the aircraft's disappearance, <a href="/wiki/Eurocontrol" title="Eurocontrol">Eurocontrol</a> issued a notice to all operators along the route that because of technical problems all flights would be tactically re-routed. The notice was retracted shortly thereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ah_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-ah-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unnamed Egyptian authorities indicated that the first parts of the wreckage had been located.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ah_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-ah-3">[3]</a></sup> Fifty ambulances were sent to the crash site<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blive_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-blive-35">[31]</a></sup> near Housna, 300 kilometres (190 mi) from Sharm El Sheikh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[35]</a></sup> Unnamed Egyptian officials reported that the aircraft "split in two" and most bodies were found strapped to their seats. Initial reports indicated that voices of trapped passengers could be heard in a section of the crashed aircraft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ElgotJohnstonKhalil2015_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-ElgotJohnstonKhalil2015-40">[36]</a></sup> At least 100 bodies were initially found, including at least five children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indept_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-indept-41">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Passengers_and_crew">Passengers and crew</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Passengers and crew">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Flight 9268 was carrying a total of 224 people, consisting of 217 passengers, of which seventeen were children, and seven crew members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mchsvictims_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-mchsvictims-6">[6]</a></sup> Most of the passengers were Russian, according to the Russian embassy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guard_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-guard-45">[41]</a></sup> and a majority were female.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[42]</a></sup> There were also four Ukrainians and one Belarusian on board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[43]</a></sup> Most of the passengers were tourists returning from <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> resorts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-48">[44]</a></sup> The Association of Tour Operators of Russia released the passenger manifest of all those thought to have been on the flight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[45]</a></sup> The majority of the passengers were from Northwest Russia, including Saint Petersburg and the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Leningrad_Oblast" title="Leningrad Oblast">Leningrad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novgorod_Oblast" title="Novgorod Oblast">Novgorod</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pskov_Oblast" title="Pskov Oblast">Pskov</a> <a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">oblasts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mchsvictims_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-mchsvictims-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Kogalymavia, the flight's <a href="/wiki/Pilot_in_command" title="Pilot in command">captain</a>, Valery Yurievich Nemov, had more than 12,000 hours of flight time, including 3,800 hours on this aircraft <a href="/wiki/Type_rating" title="Type rating">type</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ah_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-ah-3">[3]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/First_officer_(aeronautics)" title="First officer (aeronautics)">first officer</a> was Sergei Trukachev.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natalya_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-natalya-50">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many parents on the flight had left their children behind in Russia; therefore the crash orphaned multiple children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Investigation">Investigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Investigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ayman al-Muqaddam, the head of the central air traffic accident authority in Egypt, was appointed to investigate the cause of the crash. In a statement on 31 October, he indicated that the pilot had made contact with the civil aviation authorities and asked to land at the nearest airport. He suggested the aircraft may have been attempting an emergency landing at <a href="/wiki/El_Arish_International_Airport" title="El Arish International Airport">El Arish International Airport</a> in northern Sinai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guard_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-guard-45">[41]</a></sup> On the same day, Egyptian Civil Aviation Minister Hossam Kamel said that air traffic control recordings did not show any distress calls, nor change of route requests by the pilots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters-31.oct_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-31.oct-52">[48]</a></sup> The President of Egypt, <a href="/wiki/Abdel_Fattah_el-Sisi" title="Abdel Fattah el-Sisi">Abdel Fattah el-Sisi</a>, said that a probe of the crash would take months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Emergency_Situations_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Emergency Situations (Russia)">Russian Ministry of Emergency Situations</a> sent three of its aircraft to the crash site. The <a href="/wiki/Investigative_Committee_of_Russia" title="Investigative Committee of Russia">Investigative Committee of Russia</a> also started a legal case against Kogalymavia under legislation regulating "violation of rules of flights and preparations."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mchs_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-mchs-54">[50]</a></sup> Kogalymavia's employees were also questioned, along with those of the Brisco tour agency that had chartered the flight. Egyptian Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Sameh_Shoukry" title="Sameh Shoukry">Sameh Shoukry</a> promised to work closely with Russian officials and investigators to find the cause of the accident. The aircraft had passed technical checks before taking off. Investigators would also view the security camera footage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[51]</a></sup> Soon after the crash, Russia's regional transport prosecutors determined that the quality of fuel on the aircraft met required standards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>The aviation accident investigation agencies <a href="/wiki/Bureau_d%27Enqu%C3%AAtes_et_d%27Analyses_pour_la_S%C3%A9curit%C3%A9_de_l%27Aviation_Civile" title="Bureau d'Enquêtes et d'Analyses pour la Sécurité de l'Aviation Civile">BEA</a> (France), <a href="/wiki/German_Federal_Bureau_of_Aircraft_Accident_Investigation" title="German Federal Bureau of Aircraft Accident Investigation">BFU</a> (Germany), and <a href="/wiki/Air_Accident_Investigation_Unit" title="Air Accident Investigation Unit">AAIU</a> (Ireland) participated in the investigation as representatives for the state of the aircraft's design, manufacture, and registration respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BEA_investigation_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-BEA_investigation-57">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[54]</a></sup> The BEA sent two investigators, accompanied by six representatives from Airbus, to Egypt on 1 November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BEA_investigation_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-BEA_investigation-57">[53]</a></sup> According to the BEA, they joined two investigators from the BFU and four investigators from the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Aviation_Committee" title="Interstate Aviation Committee">Interstate Aviation Committee</a>, their Russian counterpart, representing the state of the aircraft's operator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BEA_investigation_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-BEA_investigation-57">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Both the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flight_data_recorder" title="Flight data recorder">flight data recorder</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cockpit_voice_recorder" title="Cockpit voice recorder">cockpit voice recorder</a> were recovered from the crash site on 1 November. Russian Transport Minister <a href="/wiki/Maksim_Sokolov" title="Maksim Sokolov">Maksim Sokolov</a> and a team of specialist investigators arrived in Cairo to assist the Egyptian investigators in determining the cause of the crash. The flight data recorders were reported to be in good condition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-59">[55]</a></sup> On 4 November, Egypt's Civil Aviation Ministry Investigators reported that the cockpit voice recorder (CVR) was partially damaged and much work was required to extract data from it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[56]</a></sup> The CVR indicated that everything was normal until a sudden disastrous event. An explosion or other sudden loud noise was heard very shortly before the recorder stopped recording.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Egyptian search and rescue team had found 163 bodies by 1 November. As the search area widened, the Egyptian team found the body of a child about 8 kilometres (5 mi) from the wreckage, indicating that the aircraft had broken up in mid-air, confirmed by Russian investigator Viktor Sorochenko.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo1_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo1-62">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>An unnamed official quoted by Reuters said that Flight 9268's tail section separated from the main body of the fuselage and was burning, which could indicate an explosion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-63">[59]</a></sup> According to a senior US defence official speaking on 2 November, a US <a href="/wiki/Infrared" title="Infrared">infrared</a> satellite detected a heat flash at the time and place of the disaster, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_intelligence_community" title="US intelligence community">US intelligence community</a> believed that it could have been an explosion on the aircraft, by either a fuel tank or a bomb and the satellite imagery also ruled out a missile attack. US Director of National Intelligence <a href="/wiki/James_R._Clapper" title="James R. Clapper">James R. Clapper</a> said that there was not yet any "direct evidence of terrorist involvement".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[60]</a></sup> Some UK news outlets reported that an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISIL" title="ISIL">ISIL</a> bomb was the most likely explanation for the crash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Within a week of the crash, serious considerations were given to the notion that the plane had been intentionally brought down. The UK government said that in the light of further British intelligence, the crash "may well have been caused by an explosive device".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbccancel_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbccancel-66">[62]</a></sup> British aviation experts travelled to Egypt to assess airport security; the UK government <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Office_Briefing_Room" title="Cabinet Office Briefing Room">Cobra</a> emergency committee, chaired by the Prime Minister, considered their findings. The BBC reported that the British government thinks the incident was probably caused by terrorism based on <a href="/wiki/Signals_intelligence" title="Signals intelligence">intercepted transmissions</a> between militants based in Sinai. These transmissions suggest that a bomb was put in the hold prior to takeoff. Although the British have not ruled out a technical fault, the BBC reports that is "increasingly unlikely".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Adams_(journalist)" title="Paul Adams (journalist)">Paul Adams</a>, BBC world affairs correspondent, said that Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>'s spokesperson left little doubt that the British government believed the aircraft was brought down by a bomb. Adams said that suspending flights both to and from a foreign country and insisting on your own technical experts assessing security demonstrated a lack of confidence in that country's own security measures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbccancel_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbccancel-66">[62]</a></sup> Security experts and investigators have said the aircraft is unlikely to have been struck from the outside and Sinai militants are not believed to have any missiles capable of striking an airliner at 30,000 ft (9,100 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the same time, flights began to be stopped from and to Sharm El Sheikh in Egypt, causing around 20,000 British tourists to be stranded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>European investigators had found that the cockpit voice recorder data is consistent with an explosion and the flight data recorder cuts off abruptly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[67]</a></sup> On 8 November, Reuters quoted an unnamed Egyptian investigation team member, speaking anonymously because of the sensitivity of the investigation, who said he was "90% sure" the airliner was brought down by a bomb, based on an initial analysis of the last second of the cockpit voice recording. Lead investigator Ayman al-Muqaddam said that other causes, such as <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">lithium batteries</a> overheating, a fuel explosion, or metal fatigue in the structure, still needed to be definitively ruled out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto4_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 November 2015, the Russian security service chief <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Bortnikov" title="Alexander Bortnikov">Alexander Bortnikov</a> announced that their investigation had concluded that a "terror act" brought down Metrojet Flight 9268 after traces of explosives were found in the wreckage. <a href="/wiki/Spectroscopy" title="Spectroscopy">Spectral analysis</a> was used among other methods to examine the substance found.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[68]</a></sup> According to Russian officials, an <a href="/wiki/Improvised_explosive_device" title="Improvised explosive device">improvised explosive device</a> with <a href="/wiki/TNT_equivalent" title="TNT equivalent">power equivalent</a> to up to 1 kilogram of <a href="/wiki/Trinitrotoluene" title="Trinitrotoluene">TNT</a> brought down the flight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crash-bomb-jet_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-crash-bomb-jet-73">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbc3322272_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbc3322272-74">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FSB3_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FSB3-75">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FSB1_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FSB1-76">[72]</a></sup> Russia offered a US$50 million reward for further information.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FSB3_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-FSB3-75">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FSB2_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FSB2-77">[73]</a></sup> Reuters reported that, according to security sources, two employees of Egypt's Sharm El Sheikh airport had been detained for questioning over the crash on suspicion of putting a bomb on board the flight. Egyptian authorities denied this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters.com_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-78">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 November 2015, ISIL published pictures of what it claimed was the bomb in its <i><a href="/wiki/Dabiq_(magazine)" title="Dabiq (magazine)">Dabiq</a></i> online magazine, claiming to show the three <a href="/wiki/Improvised_explosive_device" title="Improvised explosive device">IED</a> components including a <a href="/wiki/Schweppes" title="Schweppes">Schweppes</a> soda can containing the explosive charge, a military-grade detonator and switch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBTB_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-IBTB-20">[16]</a></sup> In the same month Russian Defense Minister <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Shoygu" title="Sergey Shoygu">Sergey Shoygu</a> announced that the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant_%E2%80%93_Sinai_Province" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant – Sinai Province">Sinai branch of ISIL</a> was responsible for downing of the flight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 December 2015 the Egyptian committee investigating the crash issued a preliminary report. The leader of the committee said that it had so far found "no evidence that there is an act of terror or illegal intervention".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[77]</a></sup> In response to the statement by the investigating committee, Russian spokesman <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Peskov" title="Dmitry Peskov">Dmitry Peskov</a> re-iterated that "our experts concluded this was a terrorist attack".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 29 January 2016 Reuters reported, from an unnamed source, that a mechanic had been detained and was suspected of planting a bomb, which he had been given by his cousin, who was a member of ISIS. Two policemen and a <a href="/wiki/Baggage_handling_system" title="Baggage handling system">baggage-handler</a> were suspected of helping the mechanic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 February 2016, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Egypt" title="President of Egypt">Egyptian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Abdel_Fattah_el-Sisi" title="Abdel Fattah el-Sisi">Abdel Fattah el-Sisi</a> acknowledged that terrorism caused the crash, saying, "Has terrorism ended? No... Whoever downed that plane, what did he want? Just to hit tourism? No. To hit relations. To hit relations with Russia."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-el-sisi_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-el-sisi-22">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_hypotheses">Other hypotheses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Other hypotheses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tailstrike_and_maintenance_hypotheses">Tailstrike and maintenance hypotheses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tailstrike and maintenance hypotheses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Airline officials have announced that they have ruled out mechanical failure, but investigators have still not made such a determination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-63">[59]</a></sup> Natalya Trukhacheva, the ex-wife of co-pilot Sergei Trukhachev, said in an interview with <a href="/wiki/NTV_(Russia)" title="NTV (Russia)">NTV</a> that her ex-husband had complained to their daughter about the aircraft's technical state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natalya_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-natalya-50">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-copilot-wife_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-copilot-wife-84">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The aircraft involved in the crash had suffered a <a href="/wiki/Tailstrike" title="Tailstrike">tailstrike</a> while landing in Cairo fourteen years earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asn_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-asn-28">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-63">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001Accident_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-2001Accident-85">[81]</a></sup> Some have drawn comparisons to <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines_Flight_123" title="Japan Airlines Flight 123">Japan Airlines Flight 123</a>, which crashed into a mountain in 1985, seven years after the aircraft had suffered a tailstrike while landing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_63-3"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-63">[59]</a></sup> Flight 123 suffered catastrophic damage in mid-air while climbing to its cruising altitude. The crash of Flight 123 was caused by an incorrect repair of the aircraft's <a href="/wiki/Empennage" title="Empennage">tail section</a> following the tailstrike, which left the <a href="/wiki/Aft_pressure_bulkhead" title="Aft pressure bulkhead">rear pressure bulkhead</a> of the airliner vulnerable to <a href="/wiki/Fatigue_(material)" title="Fatigue (material)">metal fatigue</a> and ultimately resulted in <a href="/wiki/Uncontrolled_decompression" title="Uncontrolled decompression">explosive decompression</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_63-4"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-63">[59]</a></sup> Reports on the wreckage of Flight 9268 have suggested that a "clear break" occurred near the plane's rear pressure bulkhead, possibly indicating failure of the bulkhead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001Accident_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-2001Accident-85">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 November, Metrojet spokesman Alexander Smirnov insisted that the aircraft was 100% airworthy and that its crew was "very experienced", showing certificates the airline had received in 2014, later adding that the <a href="/wiki/Tailstrike" title="Tailstrike">tailstrike</a> incident in Cairo had been fully repaired and the engines had been inspected on 26 October, five days before the crash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Missile_hypothesis">Missile hypothesis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Missile hypothesis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In a report by UK newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, a missile attack was "deemed unlikely" but the report stated that several airlines would avoid flying over Sinai while the crash was under investigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_63-5"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-63">[59]</a></sup> On 2 November, Metrojet spokesman Alexander Smirnov ruled out technical fault and <a href="/wiki/Pilot_error" title="Pilot error">pilot error</a> as the cause of the crash and blamed an "external force".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[84]</a></sup> ISIL's Wilayah Sinai claimed the incident was in revenge for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_military_intervention_in_the_Syrian_Civil_War" title="Russian military intervention in the Syrian Civil War">Russian air strikes against militants in Syria</a>, where IS controls territories, along with contiguous Iraqi territories. Wilayah Sinai was said not to have access to <a href="/wiki/Surface-to-air_missile" title="Surface-to-air missile">surface-to-air missiles</a> capable of hitting an aircraft at high altitude since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Man-portable_air-defence_systems" title="Man-portable air-defence systems">man-portable air-defence systems</a> (MANPADS) can rarely reach even half the cruising altitude of an airliner, but analysts could not exclude the possibility of a bomb on board the flight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Egyptian Army spokesman Mohamed Samir rebutted the claims and pointed out that the investigation was ongoing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[86]</a></sup> Russian Transport Minister Maksim Sokolov dismissed the claims as "fabrications" due to a lack of evidence from Egyptian civil aviation, from security officials and from air traffic data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[87]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_R._Clapper" title="James R. Clapper">James R. Clapper</a>, United States <a href="/wiki/Director_of_National_Intelligence" title="Director of National Intelligence">Director of National Intelligence</a>, said on 2 November that there was no evidence yet of terrorist involvement but that he would not rule it out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-92">[88]</a></sup> On the same day, a source on the committee analysing the <a href="/wiki/Flight_recorder" title="Flight recorder">flight recorders</a> said he believed that the aircraft was not struck from the outside and that the pilot did not make a <a href="/wiki/Distress_signal" title="Distress signal">distress signal</a> before it disappeared from <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">radar</a>. He based his comments on the preliminary investigation of both flight recorders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-92">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Disruption_to_air_traffic">Disruption to air traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Disruption to air traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The British government said that all flights due to leave Sharm El Sheikh for Britain were delayed as a "precautionary measure" to allow experts to assess security. <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_France%E2%80%93KLM" title="Air France–KLM">Air France–KLM</a> announced they would avoid overflying the Sinai peninsula until the cause of the accident has been determined. The United States' <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">Federal Aviation Administration</a> had previously told carriers under its jurisdiction to operate above <a href="/wiki/Flight_level" title="Flight level">FL260</a> (26,000 feet) while flying over Sinai. Germany's <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrt-Bundesamt" title="Luftfahrt-Bundesamt">Luftfahrt-Bundesamt</a> had told its airlines the same thing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ah_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-ah-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Air_Arabia" title="Air Arabia">Air Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flydubai" title="Flydubai">Flydubai</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> also stopped their flights over the Sinai Peninsula in response to the crash. The latter stated that they planned to continue flights over Sinai, although the intended alternative route was not announced. <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a> initially stated that they would not halt their flights to and from <a href="/wiki/Sharm_El_Sheikh" title="Sharm El Sheikh">Sharm El Sheikh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurghada" title="Hurghada">Hurghada</a>, but would actively review them; passengers who opted not to fly the route would be re-booked on another flight or given a flight voucher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-59">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 November, the British <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">Foreign and Commonwealth Office</a> (FCO) changed their travel advice to advise against all but essential travel by air to Sharm El Sheikh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph20151105_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph20151105-93">[89]</a></sup> As a result, all British flights to and from the resort were cancelled from 4 November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[91]</a></sup> On the same day, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Aviation_Authority" title="Irish Aviation Authority">Irish Aviation Authority</a> (IAA) issued an order to all Irish airline operators not to operate to or from Sharm el‐Sheikh or fly over the Sinai Peninsula until further notice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbccancel_66-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbccancel-66">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>The decisions on 4 November by the British and Irish authorities to ground flights to and from Sharm El Sheikh came within minutes of each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US-UK_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-US-UK-21">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Patrick_McLoughlin" title="Patrick McLoughlin">Patrick McLoughlin</a> – UK <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Transport" title="Secretary of State for Transport">Secretary of State for Transport</a> – told Parliament that Ireland had investigators from the <a href="/wiki/Air_Accident_Investigation_Unit" title="Air Accident Investigation Unit">Air Accident Investigation Unit</a> (AAIU) on the ground in Egypt reporting back to the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of Ireland">Irish government</a>, and the British and Irish governments have close security co-operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the morning of 5 November <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_France-KLM" title="Air France-KLM">Air France-KLM</a> announced that it would not allow hold baggage on its flight out from Cairo that day; over half of the booked passengers refused to fly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[94]</a></sup> There were an estimated 20,000 British citizens in Sharm El Sheikh on 5 November, almost half of whom were on holiday and stranded by the cancellation of flights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC05_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC05-100">[96]</a></sup> Flights to the UK were allowed again from 6 November, to enable people to travel home, but with restrictions and increased security measures. Passengers were permitted to travel home with only hand luggage, with hold luggage to be returned following a more stringent screening process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[97]</a></sup> British officials at the airport provided extra security and approved aircraft as safe to travel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC05_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC05-100">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> announced on 6 November that all Russian flights to and from Egypt were cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[100]</a></sup> Most British airlines serving the resort sent repatriation flights out to the resort to bring stranded British tourists back to the United Kingdom. On the afternoon of 6 November, Egyptian authorities placed restrictions on the number of flights due to overcrowding in the terminals; as a result, only eight of the planned 29 repatriation flights were able to leave on the day with various flights forced to divert or return to the UK whilst in the air.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sky.com_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-sky.com-105">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 8 November about 11,000 Russian tourists and about 5,300 British tourists had been flown back from the resort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 November, British airlines announced that all flights to the resort had been cancelled until at least 25 November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[107]</a></sup> The British government and head of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emirates_Airlines" title="Emirates Airlines">Emirates Airlines</a> stated that airport security throughout the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> could be significantly overhauled as a result of the bombing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[108]</a></sup> By 15 November, 16,000 British tourists had been flown back from the resort since the suspension of flights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_reactions">International reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: International reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D0%BA%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B1%D1%88%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B5_%D0%90321_31.10.15.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/%D0%90%D0%BA%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B1%D1%88%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B5_%D0%90321_31.10.15.jpg/220px-%D0%90%D0%BA%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B1%D1%88%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B5_%D0%90321_31.10.15.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/%D0%90%D0%BA%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B1%D1%88%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B5_%D0%90321_31.10.15.jpg/330px-%D0%90%D0%BA%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B1%D1%88%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B5_%D0%90321_31.10.15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/%D0%90%D0%BA%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B1%D1%88%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B5_%D0%90321_31.10.15.jpg/440px-%D0%90%D0%BA%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B1%D1%88%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B2_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B5_%D0%90321_31.10.15.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meeting_on_investigation_into_the_crash_of_a_Russian_airliner_over_Sinai_(Kremlin,_Moscow,_2015-11-17)_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1160" data-file-width="1880" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Meeting_on_investigation_into_the_crash_of_a_Russian_airliner_over_Sinai_%28Kremlin%2C_Moscow%2C_2015-11-17%29_02.jpg/220px-Meeting_on_investigation_into_the_crash_of_a_Russian_airliner_over_Sinai_%28Kremlin%2C_Moscow%2C_2015-11-17%29_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Meeting_on_investigation_into_the_crash_of_a_Russian_airliner_over_Sinai_%28Kremlin%2C_Moscow%2C_2015-11-17%29_02.jpg/330px-Meeting_on_investigation_into_the_crash_of_a_Russian_airliner_over_Sinai_%28Kremlin%2C_Moscow%2C_2015-11-17%29_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Meeting_on_investigation_into_the_crash_of_a_Russian_airliner_over_Sinai_%28Kremlin%2C_Moscow%2C_2015-11-17%29_02.jpg/440px-Meeting_on_investigation_into_the_crash_of_a_Russian_airliner_over_Sinai_%28Kremlin%2C_Moscow%2C_2015-11-17%29_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meeting_on_investigation_into_the_crash_of_a_Russian_airliner_over_Sinai_(Kremlin,_Moscow,_2015-11-17)_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> on a meeting on the investigation of the crash</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 November 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Russia" title="Government of Russia">Government of Russia</a> grounded all the A321 aircraft flown by Kogalymavia. The Russian news agency <a href="/wiki/Interfax" title="Interfax">Interfax</a> reported that the Russian transport regulator, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rostransnadzor" title="Rostransnadzor">Rostransnadzor</a>, had requested Kogalymavia to stop flying its A321 aircraft until the cause(s) of the crash had been identified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Maria_Zakharova" title="Maria Zakharova">Maria Zakharova</a>, a spokeswoman for the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Russia)">Russian Foreign Ministry</a>, stated that the <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Russia" title="List of diplomatic missions of Russia">Russian Embassy</a> was following the events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guard_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-guard-45">[41]</a></sup> President Putin declared 1 November to be a <a href="/wiki/National_day_of_mourning" title="National day of mourning">national day of mourning</a> in Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dmitry_Konstantinovich_Kiselyov" title="Dmitry Konstantinovich Kiselyov">Dmitry Konstantinovich Kiselyov</a> blamed the crash on an alleged secret pact between America and ISIL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Initially representatives of the Russian government claimed that "there is not the slightest evidence" for a terrorist attack and especially denied any links between the crash and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_military_intervention_in_the_Syrian_Civil_War" title="Russian military intervention in the Syrian Civil War">Russian intervention in Syria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[114]</a></sup> On 17 November Russia's security chief said the cause of the attack was an act of terror, and the Russian Government offered a US$50 million reward for any information that leads to the arrest of the perpetrators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FSB2_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-FSB2-77">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Egyptian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Sherif_Ismail" title="Sherif Ismail">Sherif Ismail</a> cancelled his meetings upon hearing news of the crash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sput_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sput-30">[26]</a></sup> Hours after the crash, he was on his way to the crash site along with other ministers on a private jet, according to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Tourism_(Egypt)" title="Ministry of Tourism (Egypt)">Tourism Ministry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blive_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-blive-35">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>, as the state of aircraft registry, made an offer of assistance which was accepted by the Egyptian accident investigation authorities for the Irish <a href="/wiki/Air_Accident_Investigation_Unit" title="Air Accident Investigation Unit">Air Accident Investigation Unit</a> (AAIU) of the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Transport,_Tourism_and_Sport" title="Department of Transport, Tourism and Sport">Department of Transport, Tourism and Sport</a> to send a team consisting of an Operations/Pilot Inspector, an Engineering Inspector and a Regulatory/Operations Adviser from the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Aviation_Authority" title="Irish Aviation Authority">Irish Aviation Authority</a> (IAA) to assist in the investigation. The team flew out on an Irish military aircraft on 2 November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, which borders the Sinai peninsula, offered to assist Russia and Egypt with surveillance if needed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 4 November <a href="/wiki/List_of_intelligence_agencies_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of intelligence agencies of the United Kingdom">British Intelligence</a> became involved in the investigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph20151105_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph20151105-93">[89]</a></sup> The UK government sent extra consular staff and half a dozen military planners to Egypt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC20151105_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC20151105-121">[117]</a></sup> Egyptian President al-Sisi met then British Prime Minister Cameron in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[118]</a></sup> At a joint press conference with Cameron, President Sisi said Egypt would co-operate on improved security measures at Sharm El Sheikh airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC20151105_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC20151105-121">[117]</a></sup> Cameron and Russian President Putin also discussed the investigation into the crash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC20151105_121-2"><a href="#cite_note-BBC20151105-121">[117]</a></sup> On 5 November, the government sent diplomatic staff including British embassy staff and FCO Rapid Deployment Teams to Sharm El Sheikh airport to help British nationals home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>US President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> stated, on 5 November, that the US government was taking the incident "very seriously", knowing there was a possibility that there had been a bomb on board the flight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airbus">Airbus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Airbus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> announced they would issue more information when it became available.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blive_35-3"><a href="#cite_note-blive-35">[31]</a></sup> They also released a statement on their website confirming the aircraft's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manufacturer%27s_serial_number" title="Manufacturer's serial number">MSN</a> and engine configuration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charlie_Hebdo"><i>Charlie Hebdo</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Charlie Hebdo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 6 November French satirical weekly magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Charlie_Hebdo" title="Charlie Hebdo">Charlie Hebdo</a></i> published cartoons referencing the tragedy, one with pieces of an aircraft falling on an ISIL fighter with the caption: "Russia's air force intensifies its bombing." The cartoon caused great offence in Russia and a spokesman for President Vladimir Putin called the artwork "sacrilege", and members of the <a href="/wiki/State_Duma" title="State Duma">State Duma</a> called for the magazine to be banned as extremist literature and demanded an apology from the French government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 November the magazine published another cartoon, on its cover, equating the crash with a sex act, with a caption reading: "Crash in the Sinai: finally the sex tape." The cartoon again caused great offence in Russia. In response the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Defence (Russia)">Russian Ministry of Defence</a> published cartoons on its television channel <a href="/wiki/Zvezda_(TV_channel)" title="Zvezda (TV channel)">Zvezda</a> and its website, one of which showed magazine editor <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9rard_Biard" title="Gérard Biard">Gérard Biard</a> laughing at the magazine and saying: "Laughter extends life", with the figure of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grim_reaper" title="Grim reaper">grim reaper</a> at his side commenting: "Not in your case, Gérard. Not in your case."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[124]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metrojet_Flight_9268&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The previous deadliest Russian/<a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> air disaster was the crash of <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot_Flight_7425" title="Aeroflot Flight 7425">Aeroflot Flight 7425</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Uzbek Soviet Socialist Republic">Uzbek SSR</a> (<a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>) in 1985, in which 191 passengers and 9 crew died.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The previous deadliest air disaster in Egyptian airspace was the crash of <a href="/wiki/Flash_Airlines_Flight_604" title="Flash Airlines Flight 604">Flash Airlines Flight 604</a> shortly after takeoff from Sharm El Sheikh in 2004. All 148 aboard were killed.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The previous deadliest crash involving the Airbus A320 family was <a href="/wiki/TAM_Airlines_Flight_3054" title="TAM Airlines Flight 3054">TAM Airlines Flight 3054</a> in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, Brazil in 2007, which killed 199 people. Metrojet Flight 9268 was the second fatal and deadliest accident so far involving an Airbus A321, the first being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AirBlue_Flight_202" title="AirBlue Flight 202">AirBlue Flight 202</a> which killed 152 people.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The previous deadliest 2015 air disaster was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Murder-suicide" title="Murder-suicide">murder-suicide</a> of <a href="/wiki/Germanwings_Flight_9525" title="Germanwings Flight 9525">Germanwings Flight 9525</a>, which crashed in the <a href="/wiki/Alpes-de-Haute-Provence" title="Alpes-de-Haute-Provence">French Alps</a> killing all 150 aboard.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
